   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of missions to Mars
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:

      navigation
     </a>

      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <table cellpadding="1" style="border-style:solid; border-width:1px; border-color:#c0c0c0; background-color:#fdfdfd; text-align:left; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;">

      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
        Mars
       </a>
       and its moons have been a target for many spacecraft, with flyby, orbiter, lander and rover missions visiting the planet.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chrono_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chrono-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rusweb_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rusweb-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, two spacecraft,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Rosetta_(spacecraft)" title="Rosetta (spacecraft)">
         Rosetta
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dawn_(spacecraft)" title="Dawn (spacecraft)">
         Dawn
        </a>
       </i>
       , have made flybys to get
       <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">
        gravity assists
       </a>
       for other missions; the former en route to comet
       <a href="/wiki/67P/Churyumov%E2%80%93Gerasimenko" title="67P/Churyumov–Gerasimenko">
        67P/Churyumov–Gerasimenko
       </a>
       , and the latter en route to asteroid
       <a href="/wiki/4_Vesta" title="4 Vesta">
        4 Vesta
       </a>
       and dwarf planet
       <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">
        Ceres
       </a>
       . Three missions were dedicated to
       <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">
        Phobos
       </a>
       , but they did not achieve their targets. A number of Mars orbiters include some study of Martian system especially imaging Phobos and Deimos, but there has been no dedicated mission to Deimos
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Locations_of_selected_Mars_landers_and_rovers">
        Locations of selected Mars landers and rovers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_missions_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Locations of selected Mars landers and rovers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

          <img alt="Map of Mars" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="613" height="350" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1d/Mars_Map.JPG" usemap="#ImageMap_1_677334307" width="613"/>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Map.JPG" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          <a href="/wiki/Image_map" title="Image map">
           Interactive imagemap
          </a>
          of the
          <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mars" title="Geography of Mars">
           global topography of Mars
          </a>
          , overlain with
          <a href="/wiki/List_of_artificial_objects_on_Mars" title="List of artificial objects on Mars">
           locations of Mars landers and rovers
          </a>
          (Red label =
          <a href="/wiki/Mars_rover" title="Mars rover">
           Rover
          </a>
          ; Blue label =
          <a href="/wiki/Mars_landing" title="Mars landing">
           Lander
          </a>
          ; bold red/blue = currently active). Hover your mouse to see the names of over 25
          <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mars" title="Geography of Mars">
           prominent geographic features
          </a>
          , and click to link to them. Coloring of the base map indicates relative
          <a href="/wiki/Elevation" title="Elevation">
           elevations
          </a>
          , based on data from the
          <a href="/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Laser_Altimeter" title="Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter">
           Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter
          </a>
          on NASA's
          <a href="/wiki/Mars_Global_Surveyor" title="Mars Global Surveyor">
           Mars Global Surveyor
          </a>
          . Reds and pinks are higher elevation (+3 km to +8 km); yellow is 0 km; greens and blues are lower elevation (down to −8 km). Whites (&gt;+12 km) and browns (&gt;+8 km) are the highest elevations.
          <a href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinate_system" title="Cartesian coordinate system">
           Axes
          </a>
          are
          <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
           latitude
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">
           longitude
          </a>
          ;
          <a href="/wiki/Geographical_pole" title="Geographical pole">
           Poles
          </a>
          are not shown.
          <div style="float: right;">
           <small>
            (See also:

      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <p>
       There are a number of derelict orbiters around Mars whose location is not known precisely; there is a proposal to search for small moons, dust rings, and old orbiters with the Optical Navigation Camera on the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter">
         Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There should be 8 derelict Mars orbiters barring unforeseen events if they have not decayed as of 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One example is
       <a href="/wiki/Mariner_9" title="Mariner 9">
        Mariner 9
       </a>
       , which entered Mars orbit in 1971 and is expected to remain in orbit until approximately 2022, when the spacecraft is projected to enter the Martian atmosphere and either burn up or crash into the planet's surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Viking 1 orbiter is predicted not to decay until at least 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One orbiter that is confirmed to have undergone Mars atmospheric entry is
       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Climate_Orbiter" title="Mars Climate Orbiter">
        Mars Climate Orbiter
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       (see also
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mars_orbiters" title="List of Mars orbiters">
        List of Mars orbiters
       </a>
       )
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Missions_to_the_moons_of_Mars">
        Missions to the moons of Mars
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_missions_to_Mars&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Missions to the moons of Mars">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stickney_mro.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1362" data-file-width="1836" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Stickney_mro.jpg/220px-Stickney_mro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Stickney_mro.jpg/330px-Stickney_mro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Stickney_mro.jpg/440px-Stickney_mro.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stickney_mro.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Phobos'
         <a href="/wiki/Stickney_(crater)" title="Stickney (crater)">
          Stickney Crater
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="856" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg/200px-Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg/300px-Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg/400px-Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gaspra_Phobos_Deimos.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Deimos (lower left) and Phobos (lower right) compared with the asteroid
         <a href="/wiki/951_Gaspra" title="951 Gaspra">
          951 Gaspra
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phobosmgs.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="683" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Phobosmgs.gif/210px-Phobosmgs.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Phobosmgs.gif/315px-Phobosmgs.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Phobosmgs.gif/420px-Phobosmgs.gif 2x" width="210"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phobosmgs.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Phobos by Mars Global Surveyor in 1998
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
          <a href="#cite_note-38">
           [38]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Missions dedicated to explore the two
       <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Mars" title="Moons of Mars">
        moons of Mars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">
        Phobos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Deimos_(moon)" title="Deimos (moon)">
        Deimos
       </a>
       . Many missions to Mars have also included dedicated observations of the Moons, while this section is about missions focused solely on them. There have been three unsuccessful dedicated missions and many proposals. Because of the proximity of the Mars moons to Mars, any mission to them may also be considered a mission to Mars from some perspectives.
      </p>
      <p>
       There have been at least three proposals in the United States
       <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Program" title="Discovery Program">
        Discovery Program
       </a>
       , including PADME, PANDORA, and MERLIN.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tps_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tps-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ESA has also considered a sample return mission, one of the latest known as Martian Moon Sample Return or MMSR, and it may use heritage from an asteroid sample return mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adsabs.harvard.edu_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-adsabs.harvard.edu-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 0;">

      <p>
       In Japan, the
       <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Space_and_Astronautical_Science" title="Institute of Space and Astronautical Science">
        Institute of Space and Astronautical Science
       </a>
       (ISAS) is developing a sample return mission to Phobos,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yomiuri_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-yomiuri-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       due to launch in 2024. This mission is called
       <a href="/wiki/Martian_Moons_Exploration" title="Martian Moons Exploration">
        Martian Moons Exploration
       </a>
       (MMX)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMX_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MMX-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is proposed as a flagship Strategic Large Mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       MMX will build on the expertise the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Space_Agency" title="Japanese Space Agency">
        Japanese Space Agency
       </a>
       (JAXA) would gain through the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hayabusa_2" title="Hayabusa 2">
        Hayabusa 2
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Smart_Lander_for_Investigating_Moon" title="Smart Lander for Investigating Moon">
        SLIM
       </a>
       missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of January 2018, MMX is set for launch in September 2024.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Homepage_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Homepage-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 0;">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Planned mission
        </th>
        <th>
         Target
        </th>
        <th>
         Reference
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Martian_Moons_Exploration" title="Martian Moons Exploration">
          Martian Moons Exploration
         </a>
         (MMX)
        </td>
        <td>
         Phobos and Deimos
        </td>
        <td>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMX_58-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-MMX-58">
           [58]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Three missions to land on
       <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">
        Phobos
       </a>
       have been launched; the
       <a href="/wiki/Phobos_program" title="Phobos program">
        Phobos program
       </a>
       in the late 1980s saw the launch of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fobos_1" title="Fobos 1">
        Fobos 1
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fobos_2" title="Fobos 2">
        Fobos 2
       </a>
       , while the
       <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">
        Fobos-Grunt
       </a>
       sample return mission was launched in 2011. None of these missions were successful: Fobos 1 failed en route to Mars, Fobos 2 failed shortly before landing, and Fobos-Grunt never left
       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">
        low Earth orbit
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 0;">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Launched mission
        </th>
        <th>
         Target
        </th>
        <th>
         Reference
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Phobos_1" title="Phobos 1">
          Phobos 1
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Phobos
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Phobos_2" title="Phobos 2">
          Phobos 2
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Phobos
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">
          Fobos-Grunt
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Phobos
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Missions sent to the Martian system have returned data on Phobos and Deimos and missions specifically dedicated to the moons are a subset of missions Mars that often include dedicated goals to acquire data about these moons. An example of this is the imaging campaigns by
       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Express" title="Mars Express">
        Mars Express
       </a>
       of the Mars moons.
      </p>
      <p>
       Osiris-Rex 2 was a proposal to make OR a double mission, with the other one collecting samples from the two Mars moons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2012, it was stated that this mission would be the both quickest and least expensive way to get samples from the Moons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 'Red Rocks Project', a part of Lockheed Martin's "Stepping stones to Mars" program, proposed to explore Mars robotically from Deimos.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-footstepstomars_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-footstepstomars-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
